1.  **Pricing Structure:** The Indian market primarily prices bulk aluminium profiles per kilogram (₹/kg). I found a clear price hierarchy: premium brands like Jindal command a higher price (~₹295-350/kg) compared to other brands or generic extrusions which can be as low as ₹225/kg. Alloy grade also impacts price, with 6061 often being priced higher than 6063. This confirms that `Brand` and `Alloy` are major price drivers. While I confirmed that finishes like Anodizing and Powder Coating add cost over the basic 'Mill Finish', I could not locate a standard percentage multiplier, suggesting it's context-dependent.
2.  **Regulatory Standards:** A key finding is that `IS 1285:2023` is a mandatory standard from the Bureau of Indian Standards (BIS) for general engineering profiles, and products must carry the ISI Mark to be legally sold in India. This is a critical compliance requirement for sellers. Other relevant standards for specific applications and alloys also exist (e.g., IS 733).
3.  **Market Drivers:** The demand for aluminium profiles in India is strongly tied to the health of the construction, automotive (especially the shift to EVs), and renewable energy (solar panel frames) sectors. Government programs like 'Make in India' and the 'Smart Cities Mission' are significant catalysts. I also learned that price volatility is a major market characteristic, tied to global raw material (aluminium ingot) prices and local energy costs.

- **Key Extractions:** Rationale: The evaluator has identified 'Temper' as a critical but underrepresented specification. The new sources do not provide data on this. Query: common tempers for 6063 and 6061 aluminium profiles India
- **Data Points Contributed:** 10 web results fetched
- **Agent Reasoning (Inferred):** The web search was essential to address the evaluator's feedback about the 'Temper' specification. I learned that Temper (e.g., T5, T6) is a critical attribute that defines the mechanical properties of an aluminium alloy, determined by its heat treatment. The most common combinations are `6063-T5` for architectural applications (excellent finish, good formability) and `6061-T6` for structural uses (highest strength). While I confirmed that finishes like Anodizing and Powder Coating add cost over the basic 'Mill Finish', I could not locate a standard percentage multiplier, suggesting it's context-dependent.
2.  **Regulatory Standards:** A key finding is that `IS 1285:2023` is a mandatory standard from the Bureau of Indian Standards (BIS) for general engineering profiles, and products must carry the ISI Mark to be legally sold in India. This is a critical compliance requirement for sellers. Other relevant standards for specific applications and alloys also exist (e.g., IS 733).
3.  **Market Drivers:** The demand for aluminium profiles in India is strongly tied to the health of the construction, automotive (especially the shift to EVs), and renewable energy (solar panel frames) sectors. Government programs like 'Make in India' and the 'Smart Cities Mission' are significant catalysts. I also learned that price volatility is a major market characteristic, tied to global raw material (aluminium ingot) prices and local energy costs.

I found a clear price hierarchy: premium brands like Jindal command a higher price (~₹295-350/kg) compared to other brands or generic extrusions which can be as low as ₹225/kg. This is a critical compliance requirement for sellers. Other relevant standards for specific applications and alloys also exist (e.g., IS 733).
3.  **Market Drivers:** The demand for aluminium profiles in India is strongly tied to the health of the construction, automotive (especially the shift to EVs), and renewable energy (solar panel frames) sectors. Government programs like 'Make in India' and the 'Smart Cities Mission' are significant catalysts. I also learned that price volatility is a major market characteristic, tied to global raw material (aluminium ingot) prices and local energy costs.
